Cross-Entropy Method: Pendulum Swing-Up¶

The Cross-Entropy Method (CEM) is a simple, gradient-free optimization algorithm:

  1. Sample parameter vectors from a Gaussian distribution
  2. Evaluate each by simulating the system
  3. Select the top performers ("elites")
  4. Update the distribution mean and std from the elites

No gradients needed — just simulation + sorting. We use np_cvode as the physics engine and np_randn for sampling.

In [8]:
load("numerics")$
load("numerics-sundials")$
load("ax-plots")$

1. Pendulum Dynamics¶

Simple pendulum with torque input $u$: $$\ddot{\theta} = -\frac{g}{l}\sin\theta - b\dot{\theta} + \frac{u}{ml^2}$$

Goal: swing from hanging ($\theta = \pi$) to upright ($\theta = 0$).

In [9]:
/* Pendulum parameters */
gv : 9.81$  lp : 1.0$  mp : 1.0$  bp : 0.1$

/* Max torque (saturation) */
u_max : 5.0$

2. Policy and Cost Function¶

Linear policy in features $[\sin\theta, \cos\theta, \omega]$: $$u = \text{clip}(w_1 \sin\theta + w_2 \cos\theta + w_3 \omega,\; -u_{\max},\; u_{\max})$$

These features are smooth and periodic, unlike raw $\theta$.

In [10]:
/* Cost function: simulate one episode, return scalar cost.
   Lower is better. Penalizes deviation from upright + control effort. */
simulate_cost(w1v, w2v, w3v) := block(
  [u_expr, rhs1, rhs2, tspan_sim, traj, th_col, om_col, cost_state, n_t],
  /* Build closed-loop dynamics with clipped control */
  u_expr : max(-u_max, min(u_max,
    w1v * sin(theta) + w2v * cos(theta) + w3v * omega)),
  rhs1 : omega,
  rhs2 : -(gv/lp)*sin(theta) - bp*omega + u_expr/(mp*lp^2),
  tspan_sim : np_linspace(0, 6, 300),
  /* Start hanging down: theta = pi */
  traj : np_cvode([rhs1, rhs2], [t, theta, omega],
                  [float(%pi), 0.0], tspan_sim, 1e-8, 1e-8),
  /* Cost: (1 - cos(theta))^2 + 0.1*omega^2, weighted toward final states */
  th_col : np_slice(traj, all, 1),
  om_col : np_slice(traj, all, 2),
  cost_state : np_add(
    np_pow(np_sub(1.0, np_cos(th_col)), 2),
    np_scale(0.1, np_pow(om_col, 2))),
  n_t : first(np_shape(traj)),
  float(np_mean(cost_state) + 2.0 * np_ref(cost_state, n_t - 1))
)$

/* Test: cost of zero controller (no torque, hangs at pi forever) */
print("Zero-controller cost:", simulate_cost(0.0, 0.0, 0.0))$

Zero-controller cost: 12.0

3. Cross-Entropy Method¶

Sample from $\mathcal{N}(\mu, \sigma^2)$, evaluate, select best, update. Uses np_randn for efficient batch sampling.

In [11]:
np_seed(42)$

n_params : 3$
n_samples : 40$
n_elite : 8$
n_gens : 25$

/* Initial distribution */
cem_mu : [0.0, 0.0, 0.0]$
cem_sigma : [5.0, 5.0, 5.0]$

best_cost_history : []$
mean_cost_history : []$

for gen : 1 thru n_gens do block(
  [noise, samples, costs, sorted_idx, elite_params, elite_costs,
   new_mu, new_sigma],

  /* Sample: generate [n_samples, n_params] standard normal, scale by sigma, shift by mu */
  noise : np_randn([n_samples, n_params]),
  samples : makelist(
    makelist(float(cem_mu[j] + cem_sigma[j] * np_ref(noise, i, j-1)), j, 1, n_params),
    i, 0, n_samples - 1),

  /* Evaluate each candidate (the expensive part: one ODE solve per sample) */
  costs : makelist(
    block([s], s : samples[i],
      errcatch(simulate_cost(s[1], s[2], s[3]))),
    i, 1, n_samples),
  /* Replace failed simulations with high cost */
  costs : map(lambda([c], if c = [] then 100.0 else first(c)), costs),

  /* Sort by cost, select elites */
  sorted_idx : sort(makelist(i, i, 1, n_samples),
    lambda([a, b], costs[a] < costs[b])),
  elite_params : makelist(samples[sorted_idx[i]], i, 1, n_elite),
  elite_costs : makelist(costs[sorted_idx[i]], i, 1, n_elite),

  /* Update distribution from elites */
  new_mu : makelist(
    float(lsum(p[j], p, elite_params) / n_elite),
    j, 1, n_params),
  new_sigma : makelist(
    float(max(0.3, sqrt(lsum((p[j] - new_mu[j])^2, p, elite_params) / n_elite))),
    j, 1, n_params),

  cem_mu : new_mu,
  cem_sigma : new_sigma,
  best_cost_history : append(best_cost_history, [first(elite_costs)]),
  mean_cost_history : append(mean_cost_history,
    [float(lsum(c, c, elite_costs) / n_elite)]),

  if mod(gen, 5) = 0 then
    print("Gen", gen, ": best =",
          float(round(first(elite_costs) * 1000) / 1000),
          "  mu =", map(lambda([x], float(round(x * 100) / 100)), new_mu))
)$

print("Final policy: w =",
  map(lambda([x], float(round(x * 100) / 100)), cem_mu))$

4. Evaluate the Learned Policy¶

Simulate the trained controller and compare with the uncontrolled (damped free-swing) pendulum.

In [13]:
/* Simulate trained policy */
w1_opt : cem_mu[1]$  w2_opt : cem_mu[2]$  w3_opt : cem_mu[3]$
u_opt : max(-u_max, min(u_max,
  w1_opt * sin(theta) + w2_opt * cos(theta) + w3_opt * omega))$
rhs1_opt : omega$
rhs2_opt : -(gv/lp)*sin(theta) - bp*omega + u_opt/(mp*lp^2)$

tspan_eval : np_linspace(0, 10, 500)$
traj_opt : np_cvode([rhs1_opt, rhs2_opt], [t, theta, omega],
                     [float(%pi), 0.0], tspan_eval, 1e-8, 1e-8)$

/* Uncontrolled pendulum */
traj_free : np_cvode([omega, -(gv/lp)*sin(theta) - bp*omega],
                      [t, theta, omega],
                      [float(%pi), 0.0], tspan_eval, 1e-8, 1e-8)$

t_eval : np_to_list(np_slice(traj_opt, all, 0))$
th_opt_list : np_to_list(np_slice(traj_opt, all, 1))$
th_free_list : np_to_list(np_slice(traj_free, all, 1))$

/* Wrap angle to [-180, 180] degrees */
wrap_deg(a) := block([d], d : mod(a * 180/float(%pi) + 180, 360) - 180, d)$

ax_draw2d(
  line_width = 2,
  color = royalblue,
  name = "CEM policy",
  lines(t_eval, map(wrap_deg, th_opt_list)),
  color = "#aaa",
  dash = "dash",
  name = "Uncontrolled",
  lines(t_eval, map(wrap_deg, th_free_list)),
  title = "Pendulum Swing-Up: CEM vs Uncontrolled",
  xlabel = "Time (s)",
  ylabel = "theta (deg)",
  grid = true
)$

/* Phase portrait */
om_opt_list : np_to_list(np_slice(traj_opt, all, 2))$
ax_draw2d(
  line_width = 2,
  color = royalblue,
  name = "Trajectory",
  lines(map(wrap_deg, th_opt_list),
        map(lambda([a], a * 180/float(%pi)), om_opt_list)),
  marker_size = 10,
  color = tomato,
  name = "Start (hanging)",
  points([wrap_deg(float(%pi))], [0]),
  color = forestgreen,
  name = "Target (upright)",
  points([0], [0]),
  title = "Phase Portrait: Swing-Up",
  xlabel = "theta (deg)",
  ylabel = "omega (deg/s)",
  grid = true
)$

Key Takeaways¶

  • CEM is simple: no gradients, no backpropagation — just sample, evaluate, select, repeat
  • np_cvode as the environment: each CEM sample runs a full ODE simulation as its "episode"
  • Feature engineering matters: using $[\sin\theta, \cos\theta, \omega]$ instead of raw $\theta$ gives the policy smooth, periodic inputs
  • Maxima's symbolic expressions: the policy and dynamics are symbolic, compiled to efficient native code by np_cvode's expression mode — no callback overhead

For higher-dimensional problems, gradient-based methods (using np_minimize with np_compile_gradient) would be more sample-efficient.
